Nominated for Top 20 Mobile Apps in Mobily KSA Developers Award 2014.\r\n\r\n\r\nEgyptian Senet (Ancient Egypt Game).\r\nThe Mysterious Afterlife Journey And The Favorite Pastime Of The Pharaoh Tutankhamun.\r\nThe Artifact Of The World's Oldest Board Game Found In King Tut's Tomb, Beside The Golden Coffin & Sarcophagus.\r\n\r\nAfter performing opening of the mouth ceremony on your mummy by Anubis, you start your afterlife journey protected by Eye of Horus(Wadjet) to pass through the underworld realm of Osiris, challenging an invisible adversary inside an Egyptian hidden tomb in The Valley of the Queens located near the better known Valley of the Kings, on the west bank of the Nile river across from Thebes (Luxor).\r\n\r\nSenet is a board game from predynastic and ancient Egypt, it is the earliest known record of a backgammon , checkers, draughts, ludo and chess like games.\r\n\r\nThe oldest hieroglyph representing a Senet game dates to around 3500 BC.The full name of the game in Egyptian was meaning \"The game of passing\".\r\n\r\nGames have been around for thousands of years, but none are older than the ancient game of Senet, invented by the Egyptians roughly 3500 or 5000 years ago. It is believed that this two-player board game originated as a popular form of recreation with both royalty and peasantry. But by the mid-13th century BC, Senet had evolved into a more religious ritual. Some depictions from this time period forward show the game being played not by two people, but rather as a deceased player competing against an invisible adversary, interpreted by some to symbolize the deceased players own soul.\r\n\r\nThe board has become a metaphor for the afterlife with pawns moving across the board just as a soul moves through layers of the netherworld after death. Reaching the final space and leaving the board is the goal of the game, just as reaching Horus and leaving the netherworld was the goal for the Egyptians after their death for attaining rebirth with the gods Isis & Osiris, Sekhmet & Bastet holding the Egyptian Ankh or the papyrus scepter.\r\n\r\nThe game board consists of 30 squares or slots, arranged in 3 horizontal rows of 10. Pawns move from left to right through row 1, then drop down and move from right to left through row 2. Dropping down again, pawns move from left to right along row 3 and finally, off the board. The game uses the rules developed by Timothy Kendall in his 1978 work, Passing Through the Netherworld :The Meaning and Play of Senet, an Ancient Egyptian Funerary Game.\r\n\r\nThe game includes five special squares, governed by their own rules, each containing a hieroglyphic. Square 15 is the House of Rebirth; square 26 is the House of Beauty; square 27 is the House of Water: square 28 is the House of the Three Truths; square 29 is the House of Two Truths; and square 30, the last, is the House of Horus, the Egyptian falcon-god and lord of the sky.\r\n\r\nEgyptian Senet is a pharaonic challenging game that combines luck,strategy,and magic features authentic photos of ancient Egyptian temples,plus artistically crafted graphics and animation of an ancient stone game board and pieces,set in an echoing,tomb-like chamber.Ritualistic music plus sound effects of stone pieces moving recreate the atmosphere of predynastic Egypt.The App's Icon shows the Egyptian Queen Nefertari playing Senet in her tomb,she was the great wife of the pharaoh Ramesses II(Ramses)Rio. Also many Egyptian Queens have a similar photos playing Senet such as Cleopatra,Nefertiti the great royal wife of Akhenaten,and the Queen Hatshepsut the wife of Thutmose II.\r\n\r\nSupported Languages Solitaire (known simply as solitaire or patience) is the best known and played solitaire game in the world. The aim of the game is to build up four stacks of cards starting with Ace and ending with King, all of the same suit, on one of the four foundations, at which time the you will have won!\r\n\r\nThis game is a fast and simple card game. Each new hand is random and presents a new challenge. Try and beat your best score, or set a new fastest time!\r\n\r\nWe've tried to make it as simple to play as possible, you can choose click once play, click twice or drag cards at any time.\r\n\r\nHow Klondike plays:\r\nKlondike is a variant of solitaire played using one standard deck of 52 cards. After shuffling, seven ‘piles’ of cards are laid down, the first containing one card, the second containing two, and so on, up to the seventh containing seven cards. The top card of each pile begins face up and the others face down. The remaining cards form the ‘stock’ and are placed face down at the top of the screen. The four ‘foundations’ are areas at the top into which cards are moved during play.\r\n\r\nThe game is completed by moving all of the cards to the foundations at the top of the screen. There is a separate foundation for each suit, and cards must be moved there in the following order: Ace (low), 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, Jack, Queen, King (high). To achieve this, face up cards are placed in consecutive ordered piles of alternating colours with higher cards above lower cards. For example, a pile could comprise the Queen of Hearts, then Jack of Spades, then 10 of Hearts, then 9 of Clubs, then 8 of Diamonds.\r\n\r\nThe stock cards are turned face up, either one by one or in groups of three depending on the settings, to form the ‘talon’. The top card from the talon can be moved to a pile or straight to a foundation. Face up cards in a pile can be moved, either on their own or with other cards in the same pile, to another pile as long as this preserves consecutive ordered alternating colours. Empty piles can be filled with a King or a pile of cards topped by a King. When a pile is moved to reveal a face down card, it is turned face up. Cards are moved around in this way to release cards from the talon and piles to the foundations. Cards can also be moved back out of a foundation to a pile, which may release otherwise blocked cards from the talon. When all of the stock cards have been turned over, they can be ‘recycled’ (turned face down again and redrawn).\r\n\r\nCompleting the game is not always El objetivo es lograr ese punto dulce donde las preguntas no son demasiado fáciles y no demasiado difíciles de lograr los máximos beneficios.\r\n \r\nMi motivación para desarrollar matemáticas amistosas creció de mirar a mis dos hijos interactuar con varias aplicaciones de matemáticas a través de los años. Me di cuenta de que algunas aplicaciones eran demasiado duras en los niños, utilizando la puntuación negativa que dio lugar a un montón de lágrimas y frustración. Otras aplicaciones eran juegos cronometrados que ofrecían respuestas de opción múltiple. Mi preocupación con ésos era que los cabritos aprendieron presionar rápidamente los botones correctos sin mucha comprensión del tema.\r\n\r\nMatemáticas amigables se desarrolló para abordar algunas de estas preocupaciones. Con Matemáticas amigables, los niños no son cronometrados con el fin de permitirles tiempo para pensar, consolidar el conocimiento y entender verdaderamente los problemas. Las respuestas incorrectas no son penalizadas y la aplicación a menudo ofrece segundas oportunidades. Creo que este enfoque alienta el espíritu de aprendizaje y experimentación. El refuerzo positivo se utiliza, no la puntuación negativa. Esto evita que los niños formen actitudes negativas hacia las matemáticas y proteja su autoestima. El diseño visual simple de las aplicaciones ayuda a los niños a concentrarse en las matemáticas con un mínimo de distracciones, de modo que el aprendizaje puede transferirse fácilmente a las pruebas escolares y escenarios de la vida real.\r\n \r\nMatemáticas amigables proporciona a su hijo con recompensas en forma de logros coleccionables. Para obtener el mejor efecto, se anima a los padres a proporcionar refuerzo positivo adicional vinculando los logros de la aplicación con recompensas adicionales. Usted sabe mejor qué trabaja para su niño, si es dinero de bolsillo adicional, tiempo de la pantalla, llevándolos en un viaje o nada en absoluto. Cada logro se desbloquea contestando 100 preguntas correctamente, lo que se puede hacer en una sesión o dos. Idealmente, su hijo debe ser alentado a utilizar la aplicación un par de veces a la semana, por lo que 3 o 4 logros a la semana debe ser óptimo. Una vez más, se debe lograr un equilibrio aquí. Demasiado poco uso puede no proporcionar beneficios óptimos, pero demasiado uso puede resultar en actitudes negativas y fatiga. Una vez más, usted sabe mejor lo que es óptimo para su hijo.\r\n \r\nMatemáticas amigables pueden ser utilizadas por hasta cinco niños siempre y cuando estén compartiendo una computadora. Es importante que cada niño juegue bajo su \"login\" ya que la aplicación adapta las preguntas a su hijo. Si tienen dispositivos dedicados, necesitarán una licencia separada para cada niño.\r\n \r\nMatemáticas amigas le permite instalar la aplicación en varios dispositivos y el progreso seguirá a su hijo a medida que cambia los dispositivos. Por lo tanto, su hijo puede comenzar en un dispositivo y seguir jugando en otro.\r\n \r\nHe hecho todo lo posible para diseñar matemáticas amigables para requisitos especiales de accesibilidad, pero tengo recursos limitados para probar esto. Si encuentra algo que no funciona óptimamente en términos de accesibilidad, envíeme un correo electrónico para que pueda mejorarlo. ¡Tengo muchas ganas de hacerlo bien!\r\n \r\nSi encuentra errores o problemas, simplemente envíeme un correo electrónico. Por lo general, puedo solucionar problemas rápidamente.
